---
title: "12.04 wont wake after suspend"
date: 2012-05-17
forum: General Help
---

### Post by pretty_whistle on 2012-05-17
All I get is a black screen.

What this means I don't know:  
I have a laptop light that flashes when the computer is on suspend and it stays on continually when not in suspend.  When I get this black screen the light is on continually and not flashing which means that in some fashion the computer is acknowledging the lid was opened and should wake up.

So..... I can only reach the desktop if I power down manually and power it back on.

Any help is appreciated.:)

---

### Post by lolpenguin on 2012-05-17
A suspended computer is (sort of) powered off. Have you tried pressing the power button once?

---

### Post by pretty_whistle on 2012-05-17
> **lolpenguin said:**
> A suspended computer is (sort of) powered off. Have you tried pressing the power button once?
I'll try that right now.

---

### Post by pretty_whistle on 2012-05-17
All it did was shut my computer off.

Anyone?

### Post by Cavsfan on 2012-05-17
It could be a bug. I am not sure. Suspend works perfectly in 10.04.

I bet this is a bug.

### Post by Toz on 2012-05-17
Can you provide some more information:

1. The make/model of your laptop
2. The contents of the file /var/log/pm-suspend.log
3. The results of the following commands (run in a terminal window):
```
cat /proc/cmdline
lsmod
sudo lspci -vnn | grep -A10 VGA

```

And oh, perhaps its just that the screen brightness has been turned down low and has not been restored. Have you tried increasing/decreasing the screen brightness after resume?

---

### Post by lolpenguin on 2012-05-18
It is possible your computer does not support suspend. Consider Hibernate as an alternative. It is slightly slower but does not use any battery at all (unlike suspend where RAM is still active). You will at least as much swap as your RAM or it won't work.

---

### Post by pretty_whistle on 2012-05-18
> **lolpenguin said:**
> It is possible your computer does not support suspend. Consider Hibernate as an alternative. It is slightly slower but does not use any battery at all (unlike suspend where RAM is still active). You will at least as much swap as your RAM or it won't work.
It supports suspend because till I upgraded from 11.04 I was using it ok.

Hibernate gives this error:
Failure to hibernate session.
not authorized

---

### Post by pretty_whistle on 2012-05-18
I have a question.  I've seen people post long long logs as I did but their post isn't very long because they enclose the long logs in some type of tags.  How do I do that?

### Post by Cavsfan on 2012-05-18
Ouch! Edit those posts and highlight all the text and then click on the # button at the above right.
That will wrap CODE around it. That is what you want for long streams of data like that in the forum.
Or maybe you could replace the QUOTE with CODE.

---

That will wrap CODE around it. That is what you want for long streams of data like that in the forum.
Or maybe you could replace the QUOTE with CODE.

### Post by Toz on 2012-05-18
> **pretty_whistle said:**
> It supports suspend because till I upgraded from 11.04 I was using it ok.

Hibernate gives this error:
Failure to hibernate session.
not authorized

Hibernate is disabled by default in 12.04. See: [http://www.howtogeek.com/113923/how-to-re-enable-hibernate-in-ubuntu-12.04/]("http://www.howtogeek.com/113923/how-to-re-enable-hibernate-in-ubuntu-12.04/"). Also note that hibernate won't work with an encrypted swap. If you choose to encrypt your home directory during setup, then it would have encrypted your swap as well.

But lets have a look at getting suspend to work.

---

### Post by Toz on 2012-05-18
A couple of things from your log files:

1. pm-suspend.log shows that sometimes the resume works. Is this the case or does it always fail?

2. Can you try the **pci=nomsi** kernel parameter?

3. You seen to be using the noveau driver for your nvidia card. Have you tried installing the proprietary driver? Proprietary drivers tend to be more successful with suspend functions.

---

### Post by Toz on 2012-05-18
Lets try the **pci=nomsi** kernel parameter first:

1. Open the /etc/default/grub file for editing:
```
gksudo gedit /etc/default/grub
```

2. Locate the line that starts "GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX_DEFAULT" and towards the end of the line you will have something like: > ="quiet splash"

3. Add **pci=nomsi** after splash so it looks like:
> GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX_DEFAULT="quiet splash pci=nomsi"
***Note that your line may look different than mine. All we are doing are adding one parameter after the word splash. Feel free to post back the contents of your /etc/default/grub file if you want to confirm before proceeding.

4. Save the file

5. Run:
```
sudo update-grub
```
...to recreate grub and reboot to test.

---

### Post by pretty_whistle on 2012-05-18
> **Toz said:**
> Lets try the **pci=nomsi** kernel parameter first:

1. Open the /etc/default/grub file for editing:
```
gksudo gedit /etc/default/grub
```

2. Locate the line that starts "GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX_DEFAULT" and towards the end of the line you will have something like: 

3. Add **pci=nomsi** after splash so it looks like:

***Note that your line may look different than mine. All we are doing are adding one parameter after the word splash. Feel free to post back the contents of your /etc/default/grub file if you want to confirm before proceeding.

4. Save the file

5. Run:
```
sudo update-grub
```
...to recreate grub and reboot to test.

You said, "Feel free to post back the contents of your /etc/default/grub file if you want to confirm before proceeding."  Here it is.........

```
# If you change this file, run 'update-grub' afterwards to update
# /boot/grub/grub.cfg.
# For full documentation of the options in this file, see:
#   info -f grub -n 'Simple configuration'

GRUB_DEFAULT=0
GRUB_HIDDEN_TIMEOUT=0
GRUB_HIDDEN_TIMEOUT_QUIET=true
GRUB_TIMEOUT=10
GRUB_DISTRIBUTOR=`lsb_release -i -s 2> /dev/null || echo Debian`
GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX_DEFAULT="quiet splash pci=nomsi"
GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX=""

# Uncomment to enable BadRAM filtering, modify to suit your needs
# This works with Linux (no patch required) and with any kernel that obtains
# the memory map information from GRUB (GNU Mach, kernel of FreeBSD ...)
#GRUB_BADRAM="0x01234567,0xfefefefe,0x89abcdef,0xefefefef"

# Uncomment to disable graphical terminal (grub-pc only)
#GRUB_TERMINAL=console

# The resolution used on graphical terminal
# note that you can use only modes which your graphic card supports via VBE
# you can see them in real GRUB with the command `vbeinfo'
#GRUB_GFXMODE=640x480

# Uncomment if you don't want GRUB to pass "root=UUID=xxx" parameter to Linux
#GRUB_DISABLE_LINUX_UUID=true

# Uncomment to disable generation of recovery mode menu entries
#GRUB_DISABLE_RECOVERY="true"

# Uncomment to get a beep at grub start
#GRUB_INIT_TUNE="480 440 1"
```

### Post by Toz on 2012-05-18
Ok, lets go deeper down the rabbit hole. Lets get a more detailed log file:
```
sudo bash
mv /var/log/pm-suspend.log /var/log/pm-suspend.log.BAK
export PM_DEBUG=true
pm-suspend

```

This will create a more detailed /var/log/pm-suspend.log file. When you recover (reboot) please post back the contents of the file.

And also, please post back /var/log/dmesg.0

---

### Post by jadtech on 2012-05-18
though it is very possible this could be a bug or miss configuration some where, I can tell you  I had a dell lap top that was a bout 16 month old  started having issues bringing back from hibernation and suspend out of no where  both windows and ubuntu  no matter  ..

first I tried many  things to  repair the problem even  discovered bad sectors on  the hard drive was told that could be it but the problem persisted.. 

I found the way around this most of the time without a power down was to open the lid hit the space bar several time move the mouse though I couldn't see nothing  till the power light was on solid  then close the lid till the flash was back  when I reopened the lid it would spring back and resume on windows and in ubuntu  the password login would pop up as if there was never a problem .. 

after a few weeks of suffering with this behaviour I decided to reinstall both window 7 and ubuntu  but it helped some  after that it would come out of  hibernation first try if it was less then an hour  how ever the hard drive would go to running none stop for no know reason for 5 to 15 min making it near impossible to do anything .. 

about 6 weeks after reinstalling  everything one day the dell just stopped running  it basically ran good but wouldn't charge tested the charger it would light but had no out put when we tried  several new charger it would no longer light up or boot with or with out the battery the processor was basically dead no known reason deeper investigation showed the hard drive had so many bad sectors  nothing was recoverable ..

like I said no known reason could be found no sign of heat or damage of any sort what so ever it ran fine till the battery couldn't make it run no more it shut down and never ran again end of computer had to get a new one ..

### Post by Daughain on 2012-10-08
I installed 12.04 on a Dell Inspiron 600m, and cant find a proprietary driver for the graphics card. Any ideas where to look, or how I might find one?

---

### Post by Toz on 2012-10-08
> **Daughain said:**
> I installed 12.04 on a Dell Inspiron 600m, and cant find a proprietary driver for the graphics card. Any ideas where to look, or how I might find one?

What video card do you have? From a terminal window, run the following command and post back the results:
```
sudo lspci -vnn | grep -A12 VGA
```

If its an ATI card, I think that AMD may have dropped support for it ([http://wiki.cchtml.com/index.php/Hardware]("http://wiki.cchtml.com/index.php/Hardware")) and that's why you don't see an option to install one.

I've read in a couple of places that this is a known issue the the 600m and that setting a BIOS password is a workaround (it resets the video on resume so that you can type in a password). Might be worth a try to confirm.

---
